\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{427                             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{428   \mbox{\hyperlink{src_2base_2logging_8h_a3e1cfef60e774a81f30eaddf26a3a274}{CHECK}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_1_1internal_a0cfab207d565dcf62ebf50f3987e05de}{index}}.is\_inobject());}
\DoxyCodeLine{429 }
\DoxyCodeLine{430   \textcolor{comment}{// This method implements a "{}snapshot"{} protocol to protect against reading out}}
\DoxyCodeLine{431   \textcolor{comment}{// of bounds of an object. It's used to access a fast in-\/object property from}}
\DoxyCodeLine{432   \textcolor{comment}{// a background thread with no locking. That caller does have the guarantee}}
\DoxyCodeLine{433   \textcolor{comment}{// that a garbage collection cannot happen during its query. However, it must}}
\DoxyCodeLine{434   \textcolor{comment}{// contend with the main thread altering the object in heavy ways through}}
\DoxyCodeLine{435   \textcolor{comment}{// object migration. Specifically, the object can get smaller. Initially, this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{436   \textcolor{comment}{// may seem benign, because object migration fills the freed-\/up space with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{437   \textcolor{comment}{// FillerMap words which, even though they offer wrong values, are at}}
\DoxyCodeLine{438   \textcolor{comment}{// least tagged values.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{439 }
\DoxyCodeLine{440   \textcolor{comment}{// However, there is an additional danger. Sweeper threads may discover the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{441   \textcolor{comment}{// filler words and offer that space to the main thread for allocation. Should}}
\DoxyCodeLine{442   \textcolor{comment}{// a HeapNumber be allocated into that space while we're reading a property at}}
\DoxyCodeLine{443   \textcolor{comment}{// that location (from our out-\/of-\/date information), we risk interpreting a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{444   \textcolor{comment}{// double value as a pointer. This must be prevented.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{445   \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{446   \textcolor{comment}{// We do this by:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{447   \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{448   \textcolor{comment}{// a) Reading the map first}}
\DoxyCodeLine{449   \textcolor{comment}{// b) Reading the property with acquire semantics (but do not inspect it!)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{450   \textcolor{comment}{// c) Re-\/read the map with acquire semantics.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{451   \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{452   \textcolor{comment}{// Only if the maps match can the property be inspected. It may have a "{}wrong"{}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{453   \textcolor{comment}{// value, but it will be within the bounds of the objects instance size as}}
\DoxyCodeLine{454   \textcolor{comment}{// given by the map and it will be a valid Smi or object pointer.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{455   \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_1_1internal_a5297fd2c72981b2220e6b9a831570fb3}{Tagged<Object>}} maybe\_tagged\_object =}
\DoxyCodeLine{456       \mbox{\hyperlink{classv8_1_1internal_1_1TaggedField_aa377f11588d553283d2ea7bd31c11883}{TaggedField<Object>::Acquire\_Load}}(cage\_base, *\textcolor{keyword}{this}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_1_1internal_a0cfab207d565dcf62ebf50f3987e05de}{index}}.offset());}
\DoxyCodeLine{457   \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (original\_map != map(cage\_base, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacev8_aee4e677b8d8a86416617b3330778b98a}{kAcquireLoad}})) \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} \{\};}
